          --monorail-metadata-toggled-bg: var(--monorail-metadata-closed-bg);
        }
        mr-issue-page[codeFont] {
          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: flex-start;
          z-index: 200;
        }

          flex-grow: 1;

          flex-wrap: no-wrap;

        }

        }

            width: 100%;

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        <p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

I haven't really narrowed down what's causing this. I do think there are two questions to consider here:



<span class="line"><!---->I haven't really narrowed down what's causing this. I do think there are two questions to consider here:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





creis@: what should we be showing in the omnibox for an early committed frame when we're navigating after a crash? I think we probably should not be persisting the old URL. Even though the opener window cannot poke at the DOM anymore, the early committed crash frame is not necessarily related to the old URL either (as demonstrated by this bug).



<span class="line"><!---->creis@: what should we be showing in the omnibox for an early committed frame when we're navigating after a crash? I think we probably should not be persisting the old URL. Even though the opener window cannot poke at the DOM anymore, the early committed crash frame is not necessarily related to the old URL either (as demonstrated by this bug).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Separately, I suspect there is some bug where something is incorrectly holding on to the last thing a renderer painted. It's unclear what that is though. The reason the early committed frame isn't painting is almost certainly because of 



<span class="line"><!---->Separately, I suspect there is some bug where something is incorrectly holding on to the last thing a renderer painted. It's unclear what that is though. The reason the early committed frame isn't painting is almost certainly because of <!----></span>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:third_party/blink/renderer/core/frame/local_frame_view.cc;l=4650;drc=cec3ae634439682f480b439d3eaf11544a3429c9



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:third_party/blink/renderer/core/frame/local_frame_view.cc;l=4650;drc=cec3ae634439682f480b439d3eaf11544a3429c9"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:third_party/blink/renderer/core/frame/local_frame_view.cc;l=4650;drc=cec3ae634439682f480b439d3eaf11544a3429c9<!----></a>





 (which is tracked as 



<span class="line"><!----> (which is tracked as <!----></span>





issue 1231231



<a class="strike-through" target="_blank" href="/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1231231" title="Initial empty document in iframe doesn't paint"><!---->issue 1231231<!----></a>





).



<span class="line"><!---->).<!----></span>

The viz compositor (the thing that actually controls what's on the screen) displays a given frame until it is told to display the next one, or a blank surface (at least as far as I know). So if we never tell it to update the display surface, it won't. The browser process can talk to viz, but I have no idea how crashes are communicated around the various processes.



<span class="line"><!---->The viz compositor (the thing that actually controls what's on the screen) displays a given frame until it is told to display the next one, or a blank surface (at least as far as I know). So if we never tell it to update the display surface, it won't. The browser process can talk to viz, but I have no idea how crashes are communicated around the various processes.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Paint Holding doesn't behave any differently cross platform. Mac uses different structures for the rendered surfaces and it's possible that the core Mac libraries are doing more than the GL libraries.



<span class="line"><!---->Paint Holding doesn't behave any differently cross platform. Mac uses different structures for the rendered surfaces and it's possible that the core Mac libraries are doing more than the GL libraries.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I do have this comment in the security review for Paint Holding, which may addrewss someo f the issues here:



<span class="line"><!---->I do have this comment in the security review for Paint Holding, which may addrewss someo f the issues here:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





<verbatim>



<span class="line"><!---->&lt;verbatim&gt;<!----></span>



<br>





This feature [Paint Holding] won't affect the 4s timeout as is because the new_content_rendering_timeout_ signal goes directly to the display compositor to replace the visible surface with a fallback, regardless of what the rendering is doing. I just checked to code.



<span class="line"><!---->This feature [Paint Holding] won't affect the 4s timeout as is because the new_content_rendering_timeout_ signal goes directly to the display compositor to replace the visible surface with a fallback, regardless of what the rendering is doing. I just checked to code.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





It occurs to me that I should hook up the new_content_rendering_timeout_ to always stop deferring BeginMainFrame and Commit on the renderer as well. That way no matter what happens we'll generate and push a frame as soon as possible after the 4s. That will address some problems we have with frames never starting at all.



<span class="line"><!---->It occurs to me that I should hook up the new_content_rendering_timeout_ to always stop deferring BeginMainFrame and Commit on the renderer as well. That way no matter what happens we'll generate and push a frame as soon as possible after the 4s. That will address some problems we have with frames never starting at all.<!----></span>



<br>





</verbatim>



<span class="line"><!---->&lt;/verbatim&gt;<!----></span>

Viz will hold onto/display the previous content (Surface) submitted by the Renderer until either



<span class="line"><!---->Viz will hold onto/display the previous content (Surface) submitted by the Renderer until either<!----></span>



<br>





   - Renderer submits new content



<span class="line"><!---->   - Renderer submits new content<!----></span>



<br>





   - Browser tells Viz to evict the current Renderer content.



<span class="line"><!---->   - Browser tells Viz to evict the current Renderer content.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I would expect that a Renderer crash would trigger CompositorFrameSinkImpl::OnClientConnectionLost. But while we currently clear out the connection info, we may be keeping the Surface around.



<span class="line"><!---->I would expect that a Renderer crash would trigger CompositorFrameSinkImpl::OnClientConnectionLost. But while we currently clear out the connection info, we may be keeping the Surface around.<!----></span>

>> Presumably, during this period of time, we just use the previously rendered content? Where does the logic for retaining that live?

<br>

SurfaceManager::InvalidateFrameSinkId should be called based on the Renderer crash. IIRC this keeps the most recent Surface alive.



<span class="line"><!---->SurfaceManager::InvalidateFrameSinkId should be called based on the Renderer crash. IIRC this keeps the most recent Surface alive.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I'm not familiar with how the Browser process is told of the Renderer crash. However when the Browser re-creates the Renderer it should be updating Viz of the new connection. Which should lead to clearing the old Surface.



<span class="line"><!---->I'm not familiar with how the Browser process is told of the Renderer crash. However when the Browser re-creates the Renderer it should be updating Viz of the new connection. Which should lead to clearing the old Surface.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





>> And is there any reason this logic might operate differently on Mac vs other platforms?



<span class="line"><!---->&gt;&gt; And is there any reason this logic might operate differently on Mac vs other platforms?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





DelegatedFrameHost::EmbedSurface / DelegatedFrameHostAndroid::EmbedSurface handle telling Viz of the new Surface. However there are platform specific usage differences. Each platform has its own RenderWidgetHostViewBase implementation. So there may be a Mac edge case here.



<span class="line"><!---->DelegatedFrameHost::EmbedSurface / DelegatedFrameHostAndroid::EmbedSurface handle telling Viz of the new Surface. However there are platform specific usage differences. > What does "clearing the old surface" mean? And what happens if the new frame never generates any compositor frames?



<span class="line"><!---->&gt; What does "clearing the old surface" mean? And what happens if the new frame never generates any compositor frames?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The Browser tells Viz to stop showing the old surface, after waiting N frames. (Varies per platform/reason we are clearing). Which leads to two outcomes:



<span class="line"><!---->The Browser tells Viz to stop showing the old surface, after waiting N frames. (Varies per platform/reason we are clearing). Which leads to two outcomes:<!----></span>



<br>





  1. We get the new compositor frames. We discard the old surface from memory.



<span class="line"><!---->  1. We get the new compositor frames. We discard the old surface from memory.<!----></span>



<br>





  2. Nothing arrives by the deadline.  We discard the old surface from memory. Next VSync we show a blank region.



<span class="line"><!---->  2. Nothing arrives by the deadline.  We discard the old surface from memory. Next VSync we show a blank region.<!----></span>

Right now, there are three aspects to mitigating this bug:



<span class="line"><!---->Right now, there are three aspects to mitigating this bug:<!----></span>



<br>





1. I am working on a CL to make initial empty documents paint at least once. This will resolve the problem for non-compromised renderers.



<span class="line"><!---->1. I am working on a CL to make initial empty documents paint at least once. This will resolve the problem for non-compromised renderers.<!----></span>



<br>





2. We need to understand where the 'ghost image' in step 7 is coming from in viz. This could be a bug or something else. I am relying on jonross@ or someone else from the viz team to resolve this.



<span class="line"><!---->2. We need to understand where the 'ghost image' in step 7 is coming from in viz. This could be a bug or something else. I am relying on jonross@ or someone else from the viz team to resolve this.<!----></span>



<br>





3. Removing the early commit optimization (



<span class="line"><!---->3. Removing the early commit optimization (<!----></span>





issue 1072817



<a class="" target="_blank" href="/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1072817" title="Remove the early commit optimization"><!---->issue 1072817<!----></a>





) so we no longer have to deal with the implications of the omnibox displaying the old URL when we've already done an early commit (which may not be in a renderer for the origin of the old URL).



<span class="line"><!---->) so we no longer have to deal with the implications of the omnibox displaying the old URL when we've already done an early commit (which may not be in a renderer for the origin of the old URL).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





3 is a long-term fix.



<span class="line"><!---->3 is a long-term fix.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





1 and 2 are more short-term fixes that may not be robust to compromised renderers, but should nonetheless be done. Ideally, we land both fixes, and decide which one is simpler/safer to merge if needed.



<span class="line"><!---->1 and 2 are more short-term fixes that may not be robust to compromised renderers, but should nonetheless be done. Ideally, we land both fixes, and decide which one is simpler/safer to merge if needed.<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->Author: Jonathan Ross &lt;<!----></span>





jonross@chromium.org



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="/u/jonross@chromium.org"><!---->jonross@chromium.org<!----></a>

Date: Tue Dec 14 23:01:40 2021



<span class="line"><!---->Date: Tue Dec 14 23:01:40 2021<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Evict Fallback Surface During Failed Commit



<span class="line"><!---->Evict Fallback Surface During Failed Commit<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





RenderFrameHostManager::CommitPending can re-use an existing



<span class="line"><!---->RenderFrameHostManager::CommitPending can re-use an existing<!----></span>



<br>





RenderViewHostImpl, which can have a Fallback Surface from previous



<span class="line"><!---->RenderViewHostImpl, which can have a Fallback Surface from previous<!----></span>



<br>





navigations. When swapping it is possible that the current



<span class="line"><!---->navigations. When swapping it is possible that the current<!----></span>



<br>





RenderWidgetHostView* was deleted, such as for a Renderer crash. This



<span class="line"><!---->RenderWidgetHostView* was deleted, such as for a Renderer crash. This<!----></span>



<br>





leaves us with no current Surface to take as a new Fallback Surface.



<span class="line"><!---->leaves us with no current Surface to take as a new Fallback Surface.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





It is possible for CommitPending to be for invalid target, effectively



<span class="line"><!---->It is possible for CommitPending to be for invalid target, effectively<!----></span>



<br>





failing. RenderFrameHostManager::CommitPendingIfNecessary can also



<span class="line"><!---->failing. RenderFrameHostManager::CommitPendingIfNecessary can also<!----></span>



<br>





cancel on-going navigations.



<span class="line"><!---->cancel on-going navigations.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Previously RenderWidgetHostView* would set a timeout at the start of



<span class="line"><!---->Previously RenderWidgetHostView* would set a timeout at the start of<!----></span>



<br>





navigation, so that if navigation fails we could clear any Fallback



<span class="line"><!---->navigation, so that if navigation fails we could clear any Fallback<!----></span>



<br>





Surface. However when the above occurs there is no navigation, but we



<span class="line"><!---->Surface. However when the above occurs there is no navigation, but we<!----></span>



<br>





have the Fallback Surface from a previous navigation.



<span class="line"><!---->have the Fallback Surface from a previous navigation.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This change updates RenderFrameHostManager::CommitPending to notify its



<span class="line"><!---->This change updates RenderFrameHostManager::CommitPending to notify its<!----></span>



<br>





Delegate of this impending inability to swap Fallback Surfaces.



<span class="line"><!---->Delegate of this impending inability to swap Fallback Surfaces.<!----></span>



<br>





RenderWidgetHostView* will then clear the previous Fallback Surfaces.



<span class="line"><!---->RenderWidgetHostView* will then clear the previous Fallback Surfaces.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>

Regarding #37 I believe that regardless of the compromised/not state of the Renderer, that leaving the URL not matching is incorrect:



<span class="line"><!---->Regarding #37 I believe that regardless of the compromised/not state of the Renderer, that leaving the URL not matching is incorrect:<!----></span>



<br>





  - There is nothing stopping the Renderer from producing new frames, but with the incorrect URL



<span class="line"><!---->  - There is nothing stopping the Renderer from producing new frames, but with the incorrect URL<!----></span>



<br>





  - The Reload button reloads the current displaying URL, not the visible Renderer



<span class="line"><!---->  - The Reload button reloads the current displaying URL, not the visible Renderer<!----></span>



<br>





  - This does not match the behaviour of clicking the Back button while on a crashed Renderer. (Which does change to reflect the old Renderer becoming visible)



<span class="line"><!---->  - This does not match the behaviour of clicking the Back button while on a crashed Renderer. (Which does change to reflect the old Renderer becoming visible)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This is an inconsistent UX, with a potential path for further spoofing issues.



<span class="line"><!---->This is an inconsistent UX, with a potential path for further spoofing issues.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





The example repro in #30 was great for finding the 'ghost image'. I do feel that we need one more step to completely fix this issue. From #30 Step 6.



<span class="line"><!---->The example repro in #30 was great for finding the 'ghost image'. I do feel that we need one more step to completely fix this issue. From #30 Step 6.<!----></span>



<br>





   w.location = 'data:html,foo'



<span class="line"><!---->   w.location = 'data:html,foo'<!----></span>



<br>





This is when we attempt to navigate from the crashed '



<span class="line"><!---->This is when we attempt to navigate from the crashed '<!----></span>





https://http.cat/200



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://http.cat/200"><!---->https://http.cat/200<!----></a>





'



<span class="line"><!---->'<!----></span>





 to that invalid location. I think that when this navigation begins we need to update the URL to either match the Renderer being swapped in 



<span class="line"><!----> to that invalid location. I think that when this navigation begins we need to update the URL to either match the Renderer being swapped in <!----></span>





'



<span class="line"><!---->'<!----></span>





example.com



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://example.com"><!---->example.com<!----></a>





' or whatever URL that location would be interpreted as.



<span class="line"><!---->' or whatever URL that location would be interpreted as.<!----></span>

Status

:

<strong><!---->Status:</strong>


          


          

Fixed


          

(was: Started)


          

<br>


        




        




      

<div class="issue-diff">
        <!---->
          <strong><!---->Status:</strong>
          
          Fixed
          (was: Started)
          <br>
        <!---->
        
      </div>

<br>


    


        


      


        









I'm going to mark this as fixed because the issue as reported isn't occuring anymore. Yes, a compromised renderer could produce invalid/weird frames, but realistically, if someone has that level of control, we're already in a lot of trouble as they almost certainly have arbitrary code execution in the renderer.



<span class="line"><!---->I'm going to mark this as fixed because the issue as reported isn't occuring anymore. Yes, a compromised renderer could produce invalid/weird frames, but realistically, if someone has that level of control, we're already in a lot of trouble as they almost certainly have arbitrary code execution in the renderer.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Similarly if a server replies with 204, it can't control the content in the page: it's a no-content response.



<span class="line"><!---->Similarly if a server replies with 204, it can't control the content in the page: it's a no-content response.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





While it's possible to mess with the URL display to try to blank it out (it's pretty unclear what it should show for blocked navigations or the 204 case), that seems very likely to just open up other potential problematic interactions.



<span class="line"><!---->While it's possible to mess with the URL display to try to blank it out (it's pretty unclear what it should show for blocked navigations or the 204 case), that seems very likely to just open up other potential problematic interactions.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In the future, we hope to remove the early commit optimization; that's tracked as 



<span class="line"><!---->In the future, we hope to remove the early commit optimization; that's tracked as <!----></span>





issue 1072817



<a class="" target="_blank" href="/p/chromium/issues/detail?id=1072817" title="Remove the early commit optimization"><!---->issue 1072817<!----></a>





 and



<span class="line"><!----> and<!----></span>





 will resolve the remaining concerns here.



<span class="line"><!----> will resolve the remaining concerns here.<!----></span>

*** Boilerplate reminders! ***



<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.



<span class="line"><!---->Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.<!----></span>

          border: var(--chops-accessible-border);
          z-index: 999;
          box-shadow: 2px 3px 8px 0px hsla(0, 0%, 0%, 0.3);
          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container td {
          padding: 0.25em 8px;
          white-space: nowrap;
        }
        .screenreader-hidden {
          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;
          width: 1px;
        }
      </style>
      <div class="chops-autocomplete-container">
        <span class="screenreader-hidden" aria-live="polite">
          
        </span>
        <table hidden="">
          <tbody>
            
          </tbody>
        </table>
      </div>
    <!----></mr-autocomplete>
            </div>
          </div>
